[1mNAME[0m[m
       yum - Yellowdog Updater Modified[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1myum[0m [options] [command] [package ...][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1myum[0m  is  an  interactive,  rpm  based, package manager. It can automatically perform system updates, including[m
       dependency analysis and obsolete processing based on "repository" metadata. It can also  perform  installation[m
       of  new packages, removal of old packages and perform queries on the installed and/or available packages among[m
       many other commands/services (see below). [1myum[0m is similar to other high level package managers like apt-get and[m
       smart.[m
[m
       While  there  are some graphical interfaces directly to the [1myum[0m code, more recent graphical interface develop‚Äê[m
       ment is happening with PackageKit and the gnome-packagekit application.[m
[m
       [4mcommand[24m is one of:[m
        * install package1 [package2] [...][m
        * update [package1] [package2] [...][m
        * update-to [package1] [package2] [...][m
        * update-minimal [package1] [package2] [...][m
        * check-update[m
        * upgrade [package1] [package2] [...][m
        * upgrade-to [package1] [package2] [...][m
        * distribution-synchronization [package1] [package2] [...][m
        * remove | erase package1 [package2] [...][m

[10;1H       [1myum[0m  is  an  interactive,  rpm  based, package manager. It can automatically perform system updates, including[m
[11;1H       dependency analysis and obsolete processing based on "repository" metadata. It can also  perform  installation[m
[12;1H       of  new packages, removal of old packages and perform queries on the installed and/or available packages among[m
[13;1H       many other commands/services (see below). [1myum[0m is similar to other high level package managers like apt-get and[m
[14;1H       smart.[m
[15;1H[m
[16;1H       While  there  are some graphical interfaces directly to the [1myum[0m code, more recent graphical interface develop‚Äê[m
[17;1H       ment is happening with PackageKit and the gnome-packagekit application.[m
[18;1H[m
[19;1H       [4mcommand[24m is one of:[m
[20;1H        * install package1 [package2] [...][m
[21;1H        * update [package1] [package2] [...][m
[22;1H        * update-to [package1] [package2] [...][m
[23;1H        * update-minimal [package1] [package2] [...][m
[24;1H        * check-update[m
[25;1H        * upgrade [package1] [package2] [...][m
[26;1H        * upgrade-to [package1] [package2] [...][m
[27;1H        * distribution-synchronization [package1] [package2] [...][m
[28;1H        * remove | erase package1 [package2] [...][m
[29;1H...skipping...
        * [7mlist[27m [...][m
        * info [...][m
        * provides | whatprovides feature1 [feature2] [...][m
        * clean [ packages | metadata | expire-cache | rpmdb | plugins | all ][m
        * makecache [fast][m
        * groups [...][m
        * search string1 [string2] [...][m
        * shell [filename][m
        * resolvedep dep1 [dep2] [...][m
           (maintained for legacy reasons only - use repoquery or yum provides)[m
        * localinstall rpmfile1 [rpmfile2] [...][m
           (maintained for legacy reasons only - use install)[m
        * localupdate rpmfile1 [rpmfile2] [...][m
           (maintained for legacy reasons only - use update)[m
        * reinstall package1 [package2] [...][m
        * downgrade package1 [package2] [...][m

        * repoinfo [all|enabled|disabled][m

[m
       Unless the --help or -h option is given, one of the above commands must be present.[m
[m
       Repository configuration is honored in all operations.[m
[m
       [1minstall[0m[m
              Is  used to install the latest version of a package or group of packages while ensuring that all depen‚Äê[m
              dencies are satisfied.  (See [1mSpecifying[0m [1mpackage[0m [1mnames[0m for more information) If no package  matches  the[m
              given  package  name(s), they are assumed to be a shell glob and any matches are then installed. If the[m
              name starts with @^ then it is treated as an environment group (group install @^foo),  an  @  character[m
              and it's treated as a group (plain group install).[m
[m
              If  the  name starts with a "-" character, then a search is done within the transaction and any matches[m
              are removed. Note that Yum options use the same syntax and it may be necessary to use "--"  to  resolve[m
              any possible conflicts.[m
[m
              If  the name is a file, then install works like localinstall. If the name doesn't match a package, then[m
              package  "provides"  are   searched   (e.g.   "_sqlitecache.so()(64bit)")   as   are   file[7mlist[27ms   (Eg.[m
              "/usr/bin/yum"). Also note that for file[7mlist[27ms, wildcards will match multiple packages.[m
[m
              Because install does a lot of work to make it as easy as possible to use, there are also a few specific[m
              install commands "[1minstall-n[0m", "[1minstall-na[0m" and "[1minstall-nevra[0m". These only work on package  names,  and[m
              do not process wildcards etc.[m
[m
       [1mupdate[0m If  run  without  any  packages,  update will update every currently installed package.  If one or more[m
              packages or package globs are specified, Yum will only update  the  [7mlist[27med  packages.   While  updating[m
              packages,  [1myum[0m  will ensure that all dependencies are satisfied. (See [1mSpecifying[0m [1mpackage[0m [1mnames[0m for more[m

[1mNAME[0m[m
       grep, egrep, fgrep - print lines matching a pattern[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mgrep[0m [[4mOPTIONS[24m] [4mPATTERN[24m [[4mFILE[24m...][m
       [1mgrep[0m [[4mOPTIONS[24m] [[1m-e[0m [4mPATTERN[24m | [1m-f[0m [4mFILE[24m] [[4mFILE[24m...][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mgrep[0m  searches the named input [4mFILE[24ms (or standard input if no files are named, or if a single hyphen-minus ([1m-[0m)[m
       is given as file name) for lines containing a match to  the  given  [4mPATTERN[24m.   By  default,  [1mgrep[0m  prints  the[m
       matching lines.[m
[m
       In  addition, two variant programs [1megrep[0m and [1mfgrep[0m are available.  [1megrep[0m is the same as [1mgrep[0m [1m-E[0m.  [1mfgrep[0m is the[m
       same as [1mgrep[0m [1m-F[0m.  Direct invocation as either  [1megrep[0m  or  [1mfgrep[0m  is  deprecated,  but  is  provided  to  allow[m
       historical applications that rely on them to run unmodified.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
   [1mGeneric[0m [1mProgram[0m [1mInformation[0m[m
       [1m--help[0m Print  a  usage  message  briefly summarizing these command-line options and the bug-reporting address,[m
              then exit.[m
[m
       [1m-V[0m, [1m--version[0m[m
              Print the version number of [1mgrep[0m to the standard output stream.  This version number should be included[m
              in all bug reports (see below).[m
[m
   [1mMatcher[0m [1mSelection[0m[m
       [1m-E[0m, [1m--extended-regexp[0m[m
              Interpret [4mPATTERN[24m as an extended regular expression (ERE, see below).  ([1m-E[0m is specified by POSIX.)[m
[m
       [1m-F[0m, [1m--fixed-strings[0m, [1m--fixed-regexp[0m[m
              Interpret  [4mPATTERN[24m  as  a  list of fixed strings, separated by newlines, any of which is to be matched.[m
              ([1m-F[0m is specified by POSIX, [1m--fixed-regexp[0m is an obsoleted alias, please do not use it in new scripts.)[m
[m
       [1m-G[0m, [1m--basic-regexp[0m[m
              Interpret [4mPATTERN[24m as a basic regular expression (BRE, see below).  This is the default.[m
[7m Manual page grep(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[Kii[Knn[K[K[Kcc[Kaa[Kss[Kee[K[1;1HGREP(1)                                        General Commands Manual                                        GREP(1)[m

[2;1H[m
[3;1H[1mNAME[0m[m
[4;1H       grep, egrep, fgrep - print lines matching a pattern[m
[5;1H[m
[6;1H[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
[7;1H       [1mgrep[0m [[4mOPTIONS[24m] [4mPATTERN[24m [[4mFILE[24m...][m
[8;1H       [1mgrep[0m [[4mOPTIONS[24m] [[1m-e[0m [4mPATTERN[24m | [1m-f[0m [4mFILE[24m] [[4mFILE[24m...][m
[9;1H[m
[10;1H[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
[11;1H       [1mgrep[0m  searches the named input [4mFILE[24ms (or standard input if no files are named, or if a single hyphen-minus ([1m-[0m)[m
[12;1H       is given as file name) for lines containing a match to  the  given  [4mPATTERN[24m.   By  default,  [1mgrep[0m  prints  the[m
[13;1H       matching lines.[m
[14;1H[m
[15;1H       In  addition, two variant programs [1megrep[0m and [1mfgrep[0m are available.  [1megrep[0m is the same as [1mgrep[0m [1m-E[0m.  [1mfgrep[0m is the[m
[16;1H       same as [1mgrep[0m [1m-F[0m.  Direct invocation as either  [1megrep[0m  or  [1mfgrep[0m  is  deprecated,  but  is  provided  to  allow[m
[17;1H       historical applications that rely on them to run unmodified.[m
[18;1H[m
[19;1H[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
[20;1H   [1mGeneric[0m [1mProgram[0m [1mInformation[0m[m
[21;1H       [1m--help[0m Print  a  usage  message  briefly summarizing these command-line options and the bug-reporting address,[m
[22;1H              then exit.[m
[23;1H[m
[24;1H       [1m-V[0m, [1m--version[0m[m
[25;1H              Print the version number of [1mgrep[0m to the standard output stream.  This version number should be included[m
[26;1H              in all bug reports (see below).[m
[27;1H[m
[28;1H   [1mMatcher[0m [1mSelection[0m[m
[29;1H       [1m-E[0m, [1m--extended-regexp[0m[m
[30;1H              Interpret [4mPATTERN[24m as an extended regular expression (ERE, see below).  ([1m-E[0m is specified by POSIX.)[m
[31;1H[m
[32;1H       [1m-F[0m, [1m--fixed-strings[0m, [1m--fixed-regexp[0m[m
[33;1H              Interpret  [4mPATTERN[24m  as  a  list of fixed strings, separated by newlines, any of which is to be matched.[m
[34;1H              ([1m-F[0m is specified by POSIX, [1m--fixed-regexp[0m is an obsoleted alias, please do not use it in new scripts.)[m
[35;1H[m
[36;1H       [1m-G[0m, [1m--basic-regexp[0m[m
[37;1H              Interpret [4mPATTERN[24m as a basic regular expression (BRE, see below).  This is the default.[m
[38;1H...skipping...
       [1m-i[0m, [1m--ignore-[0m[1m[7mcase[27m[0m[m
              Ignore [7mcase[27m distinctions in both the [4mPATTERN[24m and the input files.  ([1m-i[0m is specified by POSIX.)[m
[m
       [1m-v[0m, [1m--invert-match[0m[m
              Invert the sense of matching, to select non-matching lines.  ([1m-v[0m is specified by POSIX.)[m
[m
       [1m-w[0m, [1m--word-regexp[0m[m
              Select  only  those  lines  containing  matches  that  form whole words.  The test is that the matching[m
              substring must either be at the beginning of the line, or preceded by a non-word constituent character.[m
              Similarly,  it  must  be either at the end of the line or followed by a non-word constituent character.[m
              Word-constituent characters are letters, digits, and the underscore.[m
[m
       [1m-x[0m, [1m--line-regexp[0m[m
              Select only those matches that exactly match the whole line.  ([1m-x[0m is specified by POSIX.)[m
[m
       [1m-y[0m     Obsolete synonym for [1m-i[0m.[m
[m
   [1mGeneral[0m [1mOutput[0m [1mControl[0m[m
       [1m-c[0m, [1m--count[0m[m
              Suppress normal output; instead print a count of matching lines for each  input  file.   With  the  [1m-v[0m,[m
              [1m--invert-match[0m option (see below), count non-matching lines.  ([1m-c[0m is specified by POSIX.)[m
[m
       [1m--color[0m[[1m=[0m[4mWHEN[24m], [1m--colour[0m[[1m=[0m[4mWHEN[24m][m
              Surround the matched (non-empty) strings, matching lines, context lines, file names, line numbers, byte[m
              offsets, and separators (for fields and groups of context lines) with escape sequences to display  them[m
              in  color  on  the  terminal.   The  colors  are  defined by the environment variable [1mGREP_COLORS[0m.  The[m
              deprecated environment variable [1mGREP_COLOR[0m is still supported, but its setting does not have  priority.[m
              [4mWHEN[24m is [1mnever[0m, [1malways[0m, or [1mauto[0m.[m
[m
       [1m-L[0m, [1m--files-without-match[0m[m
              Suppress  normal  output; instead print the name of each input file from which no output would normally[m
              have been printed.  The scanning will stop on the first match.[m
[m
       [1m-l[0m, [1m--files-with-matches[0m[m
              Suppress normal output; instead print the name of each input file from which output would normally have[m
              been printed.  The scanning will stop on the first match.  ([1m-l[0m is specified by POSIX.)[m

[36mINTERFACE[m=[35m$1[m [34m# The interface which is brought up or down[m

    [34m# restart the services
[m    [34m# In case this dispatcher script is called several times in a short period of time, it might happen that
[m    [34m# systemd refuses to further restart the units. Therefore we use reset-failed command to prevent it.[m
    systemctl [33m-q[m is-enabled dhcpd.service && systemctl [33mrestart[m dhcpd.service && systemctl reset-failed dhcpd.service

[?1049h[?1h=dhcpd.conf(5)                                    File Formats Manual                                    dhcpd.conf(5)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       dhcpd.conf - dhcpd configuration file[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       The dhcpd.conf file contains configuration information for [4mdhcpd,[24m the Internet Systems Consortium DHCP Server.[m
[m
       The  dhcpd.conf  file is a free-form ASCII text file.  It is parsed by the recursive-descent parser built into[m
       dhcpd.  The file may contain extra tabs and newlines for formatting purposes.  Keywords in the file are  case-[m
       insensitive.  Comments may be placed anywhere within the file (except within quotes).  Comments begin with the[m
       # character and end at the end of the line.[m
[m
       The file essentially consists of a list of statements.  Statements fall into two broad categories - parameters[m
       and declarations.[m
[m
       Parameter statements either say how to do something (e.g., how long a lease to offer), whether to do something[m
       (e.g., should dhcpd provide addresses to unknown clients), or what parameters to provide to the client  (e.g.,[m
       use gateway 220.177.244.7).[m
[m
       Declarations  are used to describe the topology of the network, to describe clients on the network, to provide[m
       addresses that can be assigned to clients, or to apply a group of parameters to a group of  declarations.   In[m
       any  group  of  parameters  and  declarations,  all parameters must be specified before any declarations which[m
       depend on those parameters may be specified.[m
[m
       Declarations about network topology include the [4mshared-network[24m and the [4msubnet[24m declarations.  If clients  on  a[m
       subnet  are  to  be assigned addresses dynamically, a [4mrange[24m declaration must appear within the [4msubnet[24m declara‚Äê[m
       tion.  For clients with statically assigned addresses, or for installations where only known clients  will  be[m
       served, each such client must have a [4mhost[24m declaration.  If parameters are to be applied to a group of declara‚Äê[m
       tions which are not related strictly on a per-subnet basis, the [4mgroup[24m declaration can be used.[m
[m
       For every subnet which will be served, and for every subnet to which the dhcp server is connected, there  must[m
       be  one  [4msubnet[24m  declaration,  which tells dhcpd how to recognize that an address is on that subnet.  A [4msubnet[24m[m
       declaration is required for each subnet even if no addresses will be dynamically allocated on that subnet.[m
[m
       Some installations have physical networks on which more than one IP subnet operates.  For example, if there is[m
       a site-wide requirement that 8-bit subnet masks be used, but a department with a single physical ethernet net‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[Kii[Kpp[Kvv[K44[K[1;1Hdhcpd.conf(5)                                    File Formats Manual                                    dhcpd.conf(5)[m

       tions for these two networks must be enclosed in a [4mshared-network[24m declaration.[m
[m
       Note that even when the [4mshared-network[24m declaration is absent, an empty one is created by the server to contain[m
       the  [4msubnet[24m  (and  any  scoped  parameters  included  in the [4msubnet[24m).  For practical purposes, this means that[m
       "stateless" DHCP clients, which are not tied to addresses (and therefore subnets) will receive the  same  con‚Äê[m
       figuration as stateful ones.[m
[m
       Some  sites  may have departments which have clients on more than one subnet, but it may be desirable to offer[m
       those clients a uniform set of parameters which are different than what would be offered to clients from other[m
       departments  on  the same subnet.  For clients which will be declared explicitly with [4mhost[24m declarations, these[m
       declarations can be enclosed in a [4mgroup[24m declaration along with the parameters which are common to that depart‚Äê[m
       ment.   For  clients whose addresses will be dynamically assigned, class declarations and conditional declara‚Äê[m
       tions may be used to group parameter assignments based on information the client sends.[m
[m
       When a client is to be booted, its boot parameters are determined by consulting that client's [4mhost[24m declaration[m
       (if  any),  and  then  consulting any [4mclass[24m declarations matching the client, followed by the [4mpool[24m, [4msubnet[24m and[m
       [4mshared-network[24m declarations for the IP address assigned to the client.   Each  of  these  declarations  itself[m
       appears  within  a  lexical scope, and all declarations at less specific lexical scopes are also consulted for[m
       client option declarations.  Scopes are never considered twice, and if parameters are declared  in  more  than[m
       one scope, the parameter declared in the most specific scope is the one that is used.[m
[m
       When  dhcpd  tries  to find a [4mhost[24m declaration for a client, it first looks for a [4mhost[24m declaration which has a[m
       [4mfixed-address[24m declaration that lists an IP address that is valid for the subnet or shared network on which the[m
       client  is  booting.   If it doesn't find any such entry, it tries to find an entry which has no [4mfixed-address[24m[m
       declaration.[m
[m
[1mEXAMPLES[0m[m
       A typical dhcpd.conf file will look something like this:[m
[m
       [4mglobal[24m [4mparameters...[24m[m
[m
       subnet 204.254.239.0 netmask 255.255.255.224 {[m
         [4msubnet-specific[24m [4mparameters...[24m[m
         range 204.254.239.10 204.254.239.30;[m
       }[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 40/1945 4% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K[m
       subnet 204.254.239.32 netmask 255.255.255.224 {[m
         [4msubnet-specific[24m [4mparameters...[24m[m
         range 204.254.239.42 204.254.239.62;[m
       }[m
[m
       subnet 204.254.239.64 netmask 255.255.255.224 {[m
         [4msubnet-specific[24m [4mparameters...[24m[m
         range 204.254.239.74 204.254.239.94;[m
       }[m
[m
       group {[m
         [4mgroup-specific[24m [4mparameters...[24m[m
         host zappo.test.isc.org {[m
           [4mhost-specific[24m [4mparameters...[24m[m
         }[m
         host beppo.test.isc.org {[m
           [4mhost-specific[24m [4mparameters...[24m[m
         }[m
         host harpo.test.isc.org {[m
           [4mhost-specific[24m [4mparameters...[24m[m
         }[m
       }[m
[m
                                                          Figure 1[m
[m
       Notice that at the beginning of the file, there's a place for global parameters.  These might be  things  like[m
       the  organization's domain name, the addresses of the name servers (if they are common to the entire organiza‚Äê[m
       tion), and so on.  So, for example:[m
[m
            option domain-name "isc.org";[m
            option domain-name-servers ns1.isc.org, ns2.isc.org;[m
[m
                                                          Figure 2[m
[m
       As you can see in Figure 2, you can specify host addresses in parameters using their domain names rather  than[m
       their  numeric  IP  addresses.  If a given hostname resolves to more than one IP address (for example, if that[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 77/1945 6% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       host has two ethernet interfaces), then where possible, both addresses are supplied to the client.[m
[m
       The most obvious reason for having subnet-specific parameters as shown in Figure 1 is  that  each  subnet,  of[m
       necessity, has its own router.  So for the first subnet, for example, there should be something like:[m
[m
            option routers 204.254.239.1;[m
[m
       Note  that  the  address here is specified numerically.  This is not required - if you have a different domain[m
       name for each interface on your router, it's perfectly legitimate to use the domain name  for  that  interface[m
       instead  of  the  numeric  address.   However,  in  many  cases there may be only one domain name for all of a[m
       router's IP addresses, and it would not be appropriate to use that name here.[m
[m
       In Figure 1 there is also a [4mgroup[24m statement, which provides common parameters for  a  set  of  three  hosts  -[m
       zappo,  beppo  and  harpo.   As  you can see, these hosts are all in the test.isc.org domain, so it might make[m
       sense for a group-specific parameter to override the domain name supplied to these hosts:[m
[m
            option domain-name "test.isc.org";[m
[m
       Also, given the domain they're in, these are probably test machines.  If we wanted to test  the  DHCP  leasing[m
       mechanism, we might set the lease timeout somewhat shorter than the default:[m
[m
            max-lease-time 120;[m
            default-lease-time 120;[m
[m
       You may have noticed that while some parameters start with the [4moption[24m keyword, some do not.  Parameters start‚Äê[m
       ing with the [4moption[24m keyword correspond to actual DHCP options, while parameters that do  not  start  with  the[m
       option keyword either control the behavior of the DHCP server (e.g., how long a lease dhcpd will give out), or[m
       specify client parameters that are not optional in the DHCP protocol (for example, server-name and filename).[m
[m
       In Figure 1, each host had [4mhost-specific[24m [4mparameters[24m.  These could include such things as the [4mhostname[24m  option,[m
       the  name  of a file to upload (the [4mfilename[24m parameter) and the address of the server from which to upload the[m
       file (the [4mnext-server[24m parameter).  In general, any parameter can appear anywhere that parameters are  allowed,[m
       and will be applied according to the scope in which the parameter appears.[m
[m
       Imagine  that you have a site with a lot of NCD X-Terminals.  These terminals come in a variety of models, and[m
       you want to specify the boot files for each model.  One way to do this would be to have host declarations  for[m
       each server and group them by model:[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 115/1945 8% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K[m
       group {[m
         filename "Xncd19r";[m
         next-server ncd-booter;[m
[m
         host ncd1 { hardware ethernet 0:c0:c3:49:2b:57; }[m
         host ncd4 { hardware ethernet 0:c0:c3:80:fc:32; }[m
         host ncd8 { hardware ethernet 0:c0:c3:22:46:81; }[m
       }[m
[m
       group {[m
         filename "Xncd19c";[m
         next-server ncd-booter;[m
[m
         host ncd2 { hardware ethernet 0:c0:c3:88:2d:81; }[m
         host ncd3 { hardware ethernet 0:c0:c3:00:14:11; }[m
       }[m
[m
       group {[m
         filename "XncdHMX";[m
         next-server ncd-booter;[m
[m
         host ncd1 { hardware ethernet 0:c0:c3:11:90:23; }[m
         host ncd4 { hardware ethernet 0:c0:c3:91:a7:8; }[m
         host ncd8 { hardware ethernet 0:c0:c3:cc:a:8f; }[m
       }[m
[m
[1mADDRESS[0m [1mPOOLS[0m[m
       The  [1mpool[0m declaration can be used to specify a pool of addresses that will be treated differently than another[m
       pool of addresses, even on the same network segment or subnet.  For example, you may want to provide  a  large[m
       set of addresses that can be assigned to DHCP clients that are registered to your DHCP server, while providing[m
       a smaller set of addresses, possibly with short lease times, that are available for unknown clients.   If  you[m
       have  a firewall, you may be able to arrange for addresses from one pool to be allowed access to the Internet,[m
       while addresses in another pool are not, thus encouraging users to register their DHCP clients.  To  do  this,[m
       you would set up a pair of pool declarations:[m
[m
       subnet 10.0.0.0 netmask 255.255.255.0 {[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 152/1945 9% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K         option routers 10.0.0.254;[m
[m
         # Unknown clients get this pool.[m
         pool {[m
           option domain-name-servers bogus.example.com;[m
           max-lease-time 300;[m
           range 10.0.0.200 10.0.0.253;[m
           allow unknown-clients;[m
         }[m
[m
         # Known clients get this pool.[m
         pool {[m
           option domain-name-servers ns1.example.com, ns2.example.com;[m
           max-lease-time 28800;[m
           range 10.0.0.5 10.0.0.199;[m
           deny unknown-clients;[m
         }[m
       }[m
[m
       It  is  also possible to set up entirely different subnets for known and unknown clients - address pools exist[m
       at the level of shared networks, so address ranges within pool declarations can be on different subnets.[m
[m
       As you can see in the preceding example, pools can have permit lists that control which  clients  are  allowed[m
       access  to the pool and which aren't.  Each entry in a pool's permit list is introduced with the [4mallow[24m or [4mdeny[24m[m
       keyword.  If a pool has a permit list, then only those clients that match specific entries on the permit  list[m
       will  be  eligible to be assigned addresses from the pool.  If a pool has a deny list, then only those clients[m
       that do not match any entries on the deny list will be eligible.   If both permit and deny lists exist  for  a[m
       pool, then only clients that match the permit list and do not match the deny list will be allowed access.[m
[m
[1mDYNAMIC[0m [1mADDRESS[0m [1mALLOCATION[0m[m
       Address  allocation  is actually only done when a client is in the INIT state and has sent a DHCPDISCOVER mes‚Äê[m
       sage.  If the client thinks it has a valid lease and sends a DHCPREQUEST to initiate or renew that lease,  the[m
       server  has  only  three  choices - it can ignore the DHCPREQUEST, send a DHCPNAK to tell the client it should[m
       stop using the address, or send a DHCPACK, telling the client to go ahead and use the address for a while.[m
[m
       If the server finds the address the client is requesting, and that address is available  to  the  client,  the[m
       server  will send a DHCPACK.  If the address is no longer available, or the client isn't permitted to have it,[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 189/1945 11% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       the server will send a DHCPNAK.  If the server knows nothing about the address, it will remain silent,  unless[m
       the  address  is  incorrect  for  the  network segment to which the client has been attached and the server is[m
       authoritative for that network segment, in which case the server will send a DHCPNAK even  though  it  doesn't[m
       know about the address.[m
[m
       There  may  be  a  host declaration matching the client's identification.  If that host declaration contains a[m
       fixed-address declaration that lists an IP address that is valid for the network segment to which  the  client[m
       is  connected.   In  this  case,  the DHCP server will never do dynamic address allocation.  In this case, the[m
       client is [4mrequired[24m to take the address specified in the host declaration.  If the client sends  a  DHCPREQUEST[m
       for some other address, the server will respond with a DHCPNAK.[m
[m
       When  the DHCP server allocates a new address for a client (remember, this only happens if the client has sent[m
       a DHCPDISCOVER), it first looks to see if the client already has a valid lease on an IP address, or  if  there[m
       is  an  old  IP  address the client had before that hasn't yet been reassigned.  In that case, the server will[m
       take that address and check it to see if the client is still permitted to use it.  If the client is no  longer[m
       permitted  to  use it, the lease is freed if the server thought it was still in use - the fact that the client[m
       has sent a DHCPDISCOVER proves to the server that the client is no longer using the lease.[m
[m
       If no existing lease is found, or if the client is forbidden to receive the existing lease,  then  the  server[m
       will  look  in  the  list of address pools for the network segment to which the client is attached for a lease[m
       that is not in use and that the client is permitted to have.   It  looks  through  each  pool  declaration  in[m
       sequence  (all [4mrange[24m declarations that appear outside of pool declarations are grouped into a single pool with[m
       no permit list).  If the permit list for the pool allows the client to be allocated an address from that pool,[m
       the  pool is examined to see if there is an address available.  If so, then the client is tentatively assigned[m
       that address.  Otherwise, the next pool is tested.  If no addresses are found that  can  be  assigned  to  the[m
       client, no response is sent to the client.[m
[m
       If  an  address  is found that the client is permitted to have, and that has never been assigned to any client[m
       before, the address is immediately allocated to the client.  If the address is available  for  allocation  but[m
       has  been  previously  assigned  to  a  different  client, the server will keep looking in hopes of finding an[m
       address that has never before been assigned to a client.[m
[m
       The DHCP server generates the list of available IP addresses from a hash table.  This means that the addresses[m
       are  not  sorted  in  any  particular  order, and so it is not possible to predict the order in which the DHCP[m
       server will allocate IP addresses.  Users of previous versions of the ISC DHCP server may have  become  accus‚Äê[m
       tomed to the DHCP server allocating IP addresses in ascending order, but this is no longer possible, and there[m
       is no way to configure this behavior with version 3 of the ISC DHCP server.[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 226/1945 13% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K[m
[1mIP[0m [1mADDRESS[0m [1mCONFLICT[0m [1mPREVENTION[0m[m
       The DHCP server checks IP addresses to see if they are in use before allocating them to clients.  It does this[m
       by  sending an ICMP Echo request message to the IP address being allocated.  If no ICMP Echo reply is received[m
       within a second, the address is assumed to be free.  This is only done for leases that have been specified  in[m
       range  statements, and only when the lease is thought by the DHCP server to be free - i.e., the DHCP server or[m
       its failover peer has not listed the lease as in use.[m
[m
       If a response is received to an ICMP Echo request, the DHCP server assumes that there is a configuration error[m
       -  the  IP  address  is in use by some host on the network that is not a DHCP client.  It marks the address as[m
       abandoned, and will not assign it to clients.[m
[m
       If a DHCP client tries to get an IP address, but none are available, but there  are  abandoned  IP  addresses,[m
       then  the  DHCP  server will attempt to reclaim an abandoned IP address.  It marks one IP address as free, and[m
       then does the same ICMP Echo request check described previously.  If there is  no  answer  to  the  ICMP  Echo[m
       request, the address is assigned to the client.[m
[m
       The  DHCP  server does not cycle through abandoned IP addresses if the first IP address it tries to reclaim is[m
       free.  Rather, when the next DHCPDISCOVER comes in from the client, it will attempt a new allocation using the[m
       same method described here, and will typically try a new IP address.[m
[m
[1mDHCP[0m [1mFAILOVER[0m[m
       This  version  of  the  ISC  DHCP  server supports the DHCP failover protocol as documented in draft-ietf-dhc-[m
       failover-12.txt.  This is not a final protocol document, and we have not done  interoperability  testing  with[m
       other  vendors'  implementations of this protocol, so you must not assume that this implementation conforms to[m
       the standard.  If you wish to use the failover protocol, make sure that both failover peers  are  running  the[m
       same version of the ISC DHCP server.[m
[m
       The  failover  protocol  allows  two DHCP servers (and no more than two) to share a common address pool.  Each[m
       server will have about half of the available IP addresses in the pool at any given time  for  allocation.   If[m
       one  server  fails,  the  other  server  will  continue to renew leases out of the pool, and will allocate new[m
       addresses out of the roughly half of available addresses that it had when communications with the other server[m
       were lost.[m
[m
       It is possible during a prolonged failure to tell the remaining server that the other server is down, in which[m
       case the remaining server will (over time) reclaim all the addresses the other server had available for  allo‚Äê[m
       cation, and begin to reuse them.  This is called putting the server into the PARTNER-DOWN state.[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 263/1945 16% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K[m
       You  can put the server into the PARTNER-DOWN state either by using the [1momshell[0m [1m(1)[0m command or by stopping the[m
       server, editing the last failover state declaration in the lease file, and restarting the server.  If you  use[m
       this last method, change the "my state" line to:[m
[m
       [1mfailover[0m [1mpeer[0m [4mname[24m [1mstate[0m [1m{[0m[m
       [1mmy[0m [1mstate[0m [1mpartner-down;[0m[m
       [1mpeer[0m [1mstate[0m [4mstate[24m [1mat[0m [4mdate[24m[1m;[0m[m
       [1m}[0m[m
[m
       It is only required to change "my state" as shown above.[m
[m
       When the other server comes back online, it should automatically detect that it has been offline and request a[m
       complete update from the server that was running in the PARTNER-DOWN state, and then both servers will  resume[m
       processing together.[m
[m
       It  is possible to get into a dangerous situation: if you put one server into the PARTNER-DOWN state, and then[m
       *that* server goes down, and the other server comes back up, the other server will not  know  that  the  first[m
       server was in the PARTNER-DOWN state, and may issue addresses previously issued by the other server to differ‚Äê[m
       ent clients, resulting in IP address conflicts.  Before putting a server into PARTNER-DOWN  state,  therefore,[m
       make [4msure[24m that the other server will not restart automatically.[m
[m
       The  failover  protocol defines a primary server role and a secondary server role.  There are some differences[m
       in how primaries and secondaries act, but most of the differences simply have to do with providing a  way  for[m
       each  peer to behave in the opposite way from the other.  So one server must be configured as primary, and the[m
       other must be configured as secondary, and it doesn't matter too much which one is which.[m
[m
[1mFAILOVER[0m [1mSTARTUP[0m[m
       When a server starts that has not previously communicated with its failover peer, it must establish communica‚Äê[m
       tions  with  its  failover  peer  and synchronize with it before it can serve clients.  This can happen either[m
       because you have just configured your DHCP servers to perform failover for the first time, or because  one  of[m
       your failover servers has failed catastrophically and lost its database.[m
[m
       The  initial  recovery  process  is designed to ensure that when one failover peer loses its database and then[m
       resynchronizes, any leases that the failed server gave out before it failed will be honored.  When the  failed[m
       server starts up, it notices that it has no saved failover state, and attempts to contact its peer.[m
[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 300/1945 18% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       When  it  has  established  contact, it asks the peer for a complete copy its peer's lease database.  The peer[m
       then sends its complete database, and sends a message indicating that it is  done.   The  failed  server  then[m
       waits until MCLT has passed, and once MCLT has passed both servers make the transition back into normal opera‚Äê[m
       tion.  This waiting period ensures that any leases the failed server may have given out while out  of  contact[m
       with its partner will have expired.[m
[m
       While  the  failed server is recovering, its partner remains in the partner-down state, which means that it is[m
       serving all clients.  The failed server provides no service at all to DHCP clients until it has made the tran‚Äê[m
       sition into normal operation.[m
[m
       In  the  case where both servers detect that they have never before communicated with their partner, they both[m
       come up in this recovery state and follow the procedure we have just described.  In this case, no service will[m
       be provided to DHCP clients until MCLT has expired.[m
[m
[1mCONFIGURING[0m [1mFAILOVER[0m[m
       In  order  to  configure failover, you need to write a peer declaration that configures the failover protocol,[m
       and you need to write peer references in each pool declaration for which you want to do failover.  You do  not[m
       have  to  do  failover  for  all  pools  on a given network segment.   You must not tell one server it's doing[m
       failover on a particular address pool and tell the other it is not.  You must  not  have  any  common  address[m
       pools on which you are not doing failover.  A pool declaration that utilizes failover would look like this:[m
[m
       pool {[m
            failover peer "foo";[m
            [4mpool[24m [4mspecific[24m [4mparameters[24m[m
       };[m
[m
       Dynamic  BOOTP leases are not compatible with failover, and, as such, you need to disallow BOOTP in pools that[m
       you are using failover for.[m
[m
       The  server currently  does very  little  sanity checking,  so if  you configure it wrong, it will just   fail[m
       in  odd ways.  I would recommend therefore that you either do  failover or don't do failover, but don't do any[m
       mixed pools.  Also,  use the same master configuration file for both  servers,  and  have   a   separate  file[m
       that  contains  the  peer declaration and includes the master file.  This will help you to avoid configuration[m
       mismatches.  As our  implementation evolves,  this will  become   less  of   a   problem.   A   basic   sample[m
       dhcpd.conf  file for  a primary server might look like this:[m
[m
       failover peer "foo" {[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 337/1945 20% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K         primary;[m
         address anthrax.rc.vix.com;[m
         port 647;[m
         peer address trantor.rc.vix.com;[m
         peer port 847;[m
         max-response-delay 60;[m
         max-unacked-updates 10;[m
         mclt 3600;[m
         split 128;[m
         load balance max seconds 3;[m
       }[m
[m
       include "/etc/dhcpd.master";[m
[m
       The statements in the peer declaration are as follows:[m
[m
       The [4mprimary[24m and [4msecondary[24m statements[m
[m
         [ [1mprimary[0m | [1msecondary[0m ][1m;[0m[m
[m
         This determines whether the server is primary or secondary, as described earlier under DHCP FAILOVER.[m
[m
       The [4maddress[24m statement[m
[m
         [1maddress[0m [4maddress[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
         The  [1maddress[0m statement declares the IP address or DNS name on which the server should listen for connections[m
         from its failover peer, and also the value to use for the DHCP Failover Protocol server identifier.  Because[m
         this value is used as an identifier, it may not be omitted.[m
[m
       The [4mpeer[24m [4maddress[24m statement[m
[m
         [1mpeer[0m [1maddress[0m [4maddress[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
         The  [1mpeer[0m  [1maddress[0m statement declares the IP address or DNS name to which the server should connect to reach[m
         its failover peer for failover messages.[m
[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 374/1945 21% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       The [4mport[24m statement[m
[m
         [1mport[0m [4mport-number[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
         The [1mport[0m statement declares the TCP port on which the server should listen for connections from its failover[m
         peer.   This  statement  may  be  omitted,  in  which case the IANA assigned port number 647 will be used by[m
         default.[m
[m
       The [4mpeer[24m [4mport[24m statement[m
[m
         [1mpeer[0m [1mport[0m [4mport-number[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
         The [1mpeer[0m [1mport[0m statement declares the TCP port to which the server should connect to reach its failover  peer[m
         for  failover messages.  This statement may be omitted, in which case the IANA assigned port number 647 will[m
         be used by default.[m
[m
       The [4mmax-response-delay[24m statement[m
[m
         [1mmax-response-delay[0m [4mseconds[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
         The [1mmax-response-delay[0m statement tells the DHCP server how many seconds may pass without receiving a message[m
         from  its  failover  peer  before it assumes that connection has failed.  This number should be small enough[m
         that a transient network failure that breaks the connection will not result in the servers being out of com‚Äê[m
         munication  for  a  long time, but large enough that the server isn't constantly making and breaking connec‚Äê[m
         tions.  This parameter must be specified.[m
[m
       The [4mmax-unacked-updates[24m statement[m
[m
         [1mmax-unacked-updates[0m [4mcount[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
         The [1mmax-unacked-updates[0m statement tells the remote DHCP server how many BNDUPD messages it can  send  before[m
         it  receives a BNDACK from the local system.  We don't have enough operational experience to say what a good[m
         value for this is, but 10 seems to work.  This parameter must be specified.[m
[m
       The [4mmclt[24m statement[m
[m
         [1mmclt[0m [4mseconds[24m[1m;[0m[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 411/1945 22% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K[m
         The [1mmclt[0m statement defines the Maximum Client Lead Time.  It must be specified on the primary, and  may  not[m
         be  specified  on  the  secondary.   This  is  the length of time for which a lease may be renewed by either[m
         failover peer without contacting the other.  The longer you set this, the longer it will take for  the  run‚Äê[m
         ning  server to recover IP addresses after moving into PARTNER-DOWN state.  The shorter you set it, the more[m
         load your servers will experience when they are not communicating.  A value of something like 3600 is proba‚Äê[m
         bly reasonable, but again bear in mind that we have no real operational experience with this.[m
[m
       The [4msplit[24m statement[m
[m
         [1msplit[0m [4mindex[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
         The  split  statement specifies the split between the primary and secondary for the purposes of load balanc‚Äê[m
         ing.  Whenever a client makes a DHCP request, the DHCP server runs a  hash  on  the  client  identification,[m
         resulting  in value from 0 to 255.  This is used as an index into a 256 bit field.  If the bit at that index[m
         is set, the primary is responsible.  If the bit at that index is not set, the secondary is responsible.  The[m
         [1msplit[0m  value  determines  how many of the leading bits are set to one.  So, in practice, higher split values[m
         will cause the primary to serve more clients than the secondary.  Lower split values, the  converse.   Legal[m
         values are between 0 and 255, of which the most reasonable is 128.[m
[m
       The [4mhba[24m statement[m
[m
         [1mhba[0m [4mcolon-separated-hex-list[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
         The  hba  statement  specifies the split between the primary and secondary as a bitmap rather than a cutoff,[m
         which theoretically allows for finer-grained control.  In practice, there is probably no need for such fine-[m
         grained control, however.  An example hba statement:[m
[m
           hba ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:[m
               00:00:00:00:00:00:00:00:00:00:00:00:00:00:00:00;[m
[m
         This is equivalent to a [1msplit[0m [1m128;[0m statement, and identical.  The following two examples are also equivalent[m
         to a [1msplit[0m of 128, but are not identical:[m
[m
           hba aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:[m
               aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:aa;[m
[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 448/1945 24% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K           hba 55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:[m
               55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55:55;[m
[m
         They are equivalent, because half the bits are set to 0, half are set to 1 (0xa and 0x5 are  1010  and  0101[m
         binary  respectively)  and  consequently  this would roughly divide the clients equally between the servers.[m
         They are not identical, because the actual peers this would load balance to each server  are  different  for[m
         each example.[m
[m
         You  must  only  have  [1msplit[0m  or [1mhba[0m defined, never both.  For most cases, the fine-grained control that [1mhba[0m[m
         offers isn't necessary, and [1msplit[0m should be used.[m
[m
       The [4mload[24m [4mbalance[24m [4mmax[24m [4mseconds[24m statement[m
[m
         [1mload[0m [1mbalance[0m [1mmax[0m [1mseconds[0m [4mseconds[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
         This statement allows you to configure a cutoff after which load balancing is disabled.  The cutoff is based[m
         on the number of seconds since the client sent its first DHCPDISCOVER or DHCPREQUEST message, and only works[m
         with clients that correctly implement the [4msecs[24m field - fortunately most clients do.   We  recommend  setting[m
         this  to  something  like 3 or 5.  The effect of this is that if one of the failover peers gets into a state[m
         where it is responding to failover messages but not responding to some client requests, the  other  failover[m
         peer will take over its client load automatically as the clients retry.[m
[m
       The [4mauto-partner-down[24m statement[m
[m
         [1mauto-partner-down[0m [4mseconds[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
         This  statement  instructs the server to initiate a timed delay upon entering the communications-interrupted[m
         state (any situation of being out-of-contact with the remote failover  peer).   At  the  conclusion  of  the[m
         timer,  the  server  will  automatically  enter the partner-down state.  This permits the server to allocate[m
         leases from the partner's free lease pool after an STOS+MCLT timer expires, which can be  dangerous  if  the[m
         partner is in fact operating at the time (the two servers will give conflicting bindings).[m
[m
         Think  very  carefully before enabling this feature.  The partner-down and communications-interrupted states[m
         are intentionally segregated because there do exist situations where a failover server can fail to  communi‚Äê[m
         cate  with  its peer, but still has the ability to receive and reply to requests from DHCP clients.  In gen‚Äê[m
         eral, this feature should only be used in those deployments where the failover  servers  are  directly  con‚Äê[m
         nected to one another, such as by a dedicated hardwired link ("a heartbeat cable").[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 485/1945 26% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K[m
         A zero value disables the auto-partner-down feature (also the default), and any positive value indicates the[m
         time in seconds to wait before automatically entering partner-down.[m
[m
       The Failover pool balance statements.[m
[m
          [1mmax-lease-misbalance[0m [4mpercentage[24m[1m;[0m[m
          [1mmax-lease-ownership[0m [4mpercentage[24m[1m;[0m[m
          [1mmin-balance[0m [4mseconds[24m[1m;[0m[m
          [1mmax-balance[0m [4mseconds[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
         This version of the DHCP Server evaluates pool balance on a schedule, rather than on demand  as  leases  are[m
         allocated.   The  latter  approach  proved  to  be slightly klunky when pool misbalanced reach total satura‚Äê[m
         tion...when any server ran out of leases to assign, it also lost its ability to notice it had run dry.[m
[m
         In order to understand pool balance, some elements of its operation first need to be defined.  First,  there[m
         are  ¬¥free¬¥ and ¬¥backup¬¥ leases.  Both of these are referred to as ¬¥free state leases¬¥.  ¬¥free¬¥ and ¬¥backup¬¥[m
         are ¬¥the free states¬¥ for the purpose of this document.  The difference is that only the primary  may  allo‚Äê[m
         cate  from  ¬¥free¬¥  leases  unless under special circumstances, and only the secondary may allocate ¬¥backup¬¥[m
         leases.[m
[m
         When pool balance is performed, the only plausible expectation is to provide a 50/50 split of the free state[m
         leases  between  the  two servers.  This is because no one can predict which server will fail, regardless of[m
         the relative load placed upon the two servers, so giving each server half the leases gives both servers  the[m
         same  amount  of ¬¥failure endurance¬¥.  Therefore, there is no way to configure any different behaviour, out‚Äê[m
         side of some very small windows we will describe shortly.[m
[m
         The first thing calculated on any pool balance run is a value referred to as ¬¥lts¬¥,  or  "Leases  To  Send".[m
         This,  simply, is the difference in the count of free and backup leases, divided by two.  For the secondary,[m
         it is the difference in the backup and free leases, divided by two.  The resulting value is signed: if it is[m
         positive, the local server is expected to hand out leases to retain a 50/50 balance.  If it is negative, the[m
         remote server would need to send leases to balance the pool.  Once the lts value reaches zero, the  pool  is[m
         perfectly balanced (give or take one lease in the case of an odd number of total free state leases).[m
[m
         The  current approach is still something of a hybrid of the old approach, marked by the presence of the [1mmax-[0m[m
         [1mlease-misbalance[0m statement.  This parameter configures what used to be a 10% fixed value  in  previous  ver‚Äê[m
         sions: if lts is less than free+backup * [1mmax-lease-misbalance[0m percent, then the server will skip balancing a[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 522/1945 29% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K         given pool (it won't bother moving any leases, even if some leases "should" be moved).  The meaning of  this[m
         value  is  also  somewhat  overloaded, however, in that it also governs the estimation of when to attempt to[m
         balance the pool (which may then also be skipped over).  The oldest leases in the free and backup states are[m
         examined.  The time they have resided in their respective queues is used as an estimate to indicate how much[m
         time it is probable it would take before the leases at the top of the list would be consumed (and thus,  how[m
         long  it  would take to use all leases in that state).  This percentage is directly multiplied by this time,[m
         and fit into the schedule if it falls within the [1mmin-balance[0m and [1mmax-balance[0m configured values.  The  sched‚Äê[m
         uled  pool  check time is only moved in a downwards direction, it is never increased.  Lastly, if the lts is[m
         more than double this number in the negative direction,  the  local  server  will  ¬¥panic¬¥  and  transmit  a[m
         Failover protocol POOLREQ message, in the hopes that the remote system will be woken up into action.[m
[m
         Once  the  lts  value  exceeds  the  [1mmax-lease-misbalance[0m percentage of total free state leases as described[m
         above, leases are moved to the remote server.  This is done in two passes.[m
[m
         In the first pass, only leases whose most recent bound client would have been served by the remote server  -[m
         according  to the Load Balance Algorithm (see above [1msplit[0m and [1mhba[0m configuration statements) - are given away[m
         to the peer.  This first pass will happily continue to give away leases, decrementing the lts value  by  one[m
         for  each, until the lts value has reached the negative of the total number of leases multiplied by the [1mmax-[0m[m
         [1mlease-ownership[0m percentage.  So it is through this value that you can permit a small misbalance of the lease[m
         pools - for the purpose of giving the peer more than a 50/50 share of leases in the hopes that their clients[m
         might some day return and be allocated by the peer (operating normally).  This process  is  referred  to  as[m
         ¬¥MAC Address Affinity¬¥, but this is somewhat misnamed: it applies equally to DHCP Client Identifier options.[m
         Note also that affinity is applied to leases when they enter the state ¬¥free¬¥ from ¬¥expired¬¥ or  ¬¥released¬¥.[m
         In  this  case also, leases will not be moved from free to backup if the secondary already has more than its[m
         share.[m
[m
         The second pass is only entered into if the first pass fails to reduce the lts underneath the  total  number[m
         of  free state leases multiplied by the [1mmax-lease-ownership[0m percentage.  In this pass, the oldest leases are[m
         given over to the peer without second thought about the Load Balance Algorithm, and this continues until the[m
         lts  falls under this value.  In this way, the local server will also happily keep a small percentage of the[m
         leases that would normally load balance to itself.[m
[m
         So, the [1mmax-lease-misbalance[0m value acts as a behavioural gate.  Smaller values will  cause  more  leases  to[m
         transition  states to balance the pools over time, higher values will decrease the amount of change (but may[m
         lead to pool starvation if there's a run on leases).[m
[m
         The [1mmax-lease-ownership[0m value permits a small (percentage) skew in the lease balance of a percentage of  the[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 559/1945 31% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K         total number of free state leases.[m
[m
         Finally, the [1mmin-balance[0m and [1mmax-balance[0m make certain that a scheduled rebalance event happens within a rea‚Äê[m
         sonable timeframe (not to be thrown off by, for example, a 7 year old free lease).[m
[m
         Plausible values for the percentages lie between 0 and 100, inclusive, but values over 50 are indistinguish‚Äê[m
         able from one another (once lts exceeds 50% of the free state leases, one server must therefore have 100% of[m
         the leases in its respective free state).  It is recommended to select a [1mmax-lease-ownership[0m value  that  is[m
         lower  than  the value selected for the [1mmax-lease-misbalance[0m value.  [1mmax-lease-ownership[0m defaults to 10, and[m
         [1mmax-lease-misbalance[0m defaults to 15.[m
[m
         Plausible values for the [1mmin-balance[0m and [1mmax-balance[0m times also range from 0 to (2^32)-1 (or  the  limit  of[m
         your  local time_t value), but default to values 60 and 3600 respectively (to place balance events between 1[m
         minute and 1 hour).[m
[m
[1mCLIENT[0m [1mCLASSING[0m[m
       Clients can be separated into classes, and treated differently depending on what class they are in.  This sep‚Äê[m
       aration  can  be done either with a conditional statement, or with a match statement within the class declara‚Äê[m
       tion.  It is possible to specify a limit on the total number of clients within a particular class or  subclass[m
       that may hold leases at one time, and it is possible to specify automatic subclassing based on the contents of[m
       the client packet.[m
[m
       To add clients to classes based on conditional evaluation, you can specify a matching expression in the  class[m
       statement:[m
[m
       class "ras-clients" {[m
         match if substring (option dhcp-client-identifier, 1, 3) = "RAS";[m
       }[m
[m
       Note  that  whether  you  use  matching  expressions or add statements (or both) to classify clients, you must[m
       always write a class declaration for any class that you use.  If there will be no match statement and  no  in-[m
       scope statements for a class, the declaration should look like this:[m
[m
       class "ras-clients" {[m
       }[m
[m
[1mSUBCLASSES[0m[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 596/1945 33% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       In  addition  to classes, it is possible to declare subclasses.  A subclass is a class with the same name as a[m
       regular class, but with a specific submatch expression which is hashed for quick  matching.   This  is  essen‚Äê[m
       tially  a speed hack - the main difference between five classes with match expressions and one class with five[m
       subclasses is that it will be quicker to find the subclasses.  Subclasses work as follows:[m
[m
       class "allocation-class-1" {[m
         match pick-first-value (option dhcp-client-identifier, hardware);[m
       }[m
[m
       class "allocation-class-2" {[m
         match pick-first-value (option dhcp-client-identifier, hardware);[m
       }[m
[m
       subclass "allocation-class-1" 1:8:0:2b:4c:39:ad;[m
       subclass "allocation-class-2" 1:8:0:2b:a9:cc:e3;[m
       subclass "allocation-class-1" 1:0:0:c4:aa:29:44;[m
[m
       subnet 10.0.0.0 netmask 255.255.255.0 {[m
         pool {[m
           allow members of "allocation-class-1";[m
           range 10.0.0.11 10.0.0.50;[m
         }[m
         pool {[m
           allow members of "allocation-class-2";[m
           range 10.0.0.51 10.0.0.100;[m
         }[m
       }[m
[m
       The data following the class name in the subclass declaration is a constant value to use in matching the match[m
       expression for the class.  When class matching is done, the server will evaluate the match expression and then[m
       look the result up in the hash table.  If it finds a match, the client is considered  a  member  of  both  the[m
       class and the subclass.[m
[m
       Subclasses  can  be declared with or without scope.  In the above example, the sole purpose of the subclass is[m
       to allow some clients access to one address pool, while other clients are given access to the other  pool,  so[m
       these subclasses are declared without scopes.  If part of the purpose of the subclass were to define different[m
       parameter values for some clients, you might want to declare some subclasses with scopes.[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 633/1945 35% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[Kii[Kpp[K[1;1H       In  addition  to classes, it is possible to declare subclasses.  A subclass is a class with the same name as a[m

[36;1H       these subclasses are declared without scopes.  If part of the purpose of the subclass were to define different[m
[37;1H       parameter values for some clients, you might want to declare some subclasses with scopes.[m
[38;1H...skipping...
       ISP wishes to provide clients at a particular site with more than one [7mIP[27m address, but does not wish to provide[m
       such clients with their own subnet, nor give them an unlimited number of [7mIP[27m addresses from the network segment[m
       to which they are connected.[m
[m
       Many cable modem head-end systems can be configured to add a Relay Agent Information option  to  DHCP  packets[m
       when  relaying  them  to  the  DHCP server.  These systems typically add a circuit ID or remote ID option that[m
       uniquely identifies the customer site.  To take advantage of this, you can write a class declaration  as  fol‚Äê[m
       lows:[m
[m
       class "customer" {[m
         spawn with option agent.circuit-id;[m
         lease limit 4;[m
       }[m
[m
       Now  whenever  a  request  comes  in  from  a customer site, the circuit ID option will be checked against the[m
       class's hash table.  If a subclass is found that matches the circuit ID, the client will be classified in that[m
       subclass  and treated accordingly.  If no subclass is found matching the circuit ID, a new one will be created[m
       and logged in the [1mdhcpd.leases[0m file, and the client will be classified in this new class.  Once the client has[m
       been  classified,  it will be treated according to the rules of the class, including, in this case, being sub‚Äê[m
       ject to the per-site limit of four leases.[m
[m
       The use of the subclass spawning mechanism is not restricted to relay agent options - this particular  example[m
       is given only because it is a fairly straightforward one.[m
[m
[1mCOMBINING[0m [1mMATCH,[0m [1mMATCH[0m [1mIF[0m [1mAND[0m [1mSPAWN[0m [1mWITH[0m[m
       In  some  cases, it may be useful to use one expression to assign a client to a particular class, and a second[m
       expression to put it into a subclass of that class.  This can be done by combining the [1mmatch[0m [1mif[0m and [1mspawn[0m [1mwith[0m[m
       statements, or the [1mmatch[0m [1mif[0m and [1mmatch[0m statements.  For example:[m
[m
       class "jr-cable-modems" {[m
         match if option dhcp-vendor-identifier = "jrcm";[m
         spawn with option agent.circuit-id;[m
         lease limit 4;[m
       }[m
[m
       class "dv-dsl-modems" {[m
         match if option dhcp-vendor-identifier = "dvdsl";[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 702/1945 38% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K         spawn with option agent.circuit-id;[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 703/1945 38% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K...skipping...
       therefore does not attempt to set up an A record for the client, but does set up  a  PTR  record  for  the  [7mIP[27m[m
       address  that  it assigns the client, pointing at jschmoe.radish.org.  Once the DHCP client has an [7mIP[27m address,[m
       it can update its own A record, assuming that the "radish.org" DNS server will allow it to do so.[m
[m
       If the server is configured not to allow client updates, or if the client doesn¬¥t want to do its  own  update,[m
       the  server  will simply choose a name for the client from either the fqdn option (if present) or the hostname[m
       option (if present).  It will use its own domain name for the client.  It will then update both the A and  PTR[m
       record, using the name that it chose for the client.  If the client sends a fully-qualified domain name in the[m
       [1mfqdn[0m option, the server uses only the leftmost part of the domain name  -  in  the  example  above,  "jschmoe"[m
       instead of "jschmoe.radish.org".[m
[m
       Further,  if the [4mignore[24m [4mclient-updates;[24m directive is used, then the server will in addition send a response in[m
       the DHCP packet, using the FQDN Option, that implies to the client that it should perform its own  updates  if[m
       it chooses to do so.  With [4mdeny[24m [4mclient-updates;[24m, a response is sent which indicates the client may not perform[m
       updates.[m
[m
       Also, if the [4muse-host-decl-names[24m configuration option is enabled, then the host declaration¬¥s [4mhostname[24m will be[m
       used in place of the [4mhostname[24m option, and the same rules will apply as described above.[m
[m
       Both  the  standard and interim options also include a method to allow more than one DHCP server to update the[m
       DNS database without accidentally deleting A records that shouldn¬¥t be deleted nor failing to  add  A  records[m
       that should be added.  For the standard option the method works as follows:[m
[m
       When  the  DHCP server issues a client a new lease, it creates a text string that is an SHA hash over the DHCP[m
       client¬¥s identification (see RFCs 4701 & 4702 for details).  The update attempts to add an A record  with  the[m
       name  the  server  chose  and a DHCID record containing the hashed identifier string (hashid).  If this update[m
       succeeds, the server is done.[m
[m
       If the update fails because the A record already exists, then the DHCP server attempts to  add  the  A  record[m
       with  the  prerequisite that there must be a DHCID record in the same name as the new A record, and that DHCID[m
       record¬¥s contents must be equal to hashid.  If this update succeeds, then the client has its A record and  PTR[m
       record.   If  it fails, then the name the client has been assigned (or requested) is in use, and can¬¥t be used[m
       by the client.  At this point the DHCP server gives up trying to do a DNS update  for  the  client  until  the[m
       client chooses a new name.[m
[m
       The  server  also does not update very aggressively.  Because each DNS update involves a round tr[7mip[27m to the DNS[m
       server, there is a cost associated with doing updates even if they do not actually modify  the  DNS  database.[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 790/1945 43% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K       So  the DHCP server tracks whether or not it has updated the record in the past (this information is stored on[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 791/1945 43% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[?1l>[?1049l]0;root@vm0:~[root@vm0 11:29:03]# man dhcpd.conf

[1mNAME[0m[m
       dhcpd.conf - dhcpd configuration file[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       The dhcpd.conf file contains configuration information for [4mdhcpd,[24m the Internet Systems Consortium DHCP Server.[m
[m
       The  dhcpd.conf  file is a free-form ASCII text file.  It is parsed by the recursive-descent parser built into[m
       dhcpd.  The file may contain extra tabs and newlines for formatting purposes.  Keywords in the file are  case-[m
       insensitive.  Comments may be placed anywhere within the file (except within quotes).  Comments begin with the[m
       # character and end at the end of the line.[m
[m
       The file essentially consists of a list of statements.  Statements fall into two broad categories - parameters[m
       and declarations.[m
[m
       Parameter statements either say how to do something (e.g., how long a lease to offer), whether to do something[m
       (e.g., should dhcpd provide addresses to unknown clients), or what parameters to provide to the client  (e.g.,[m
       use gateway 220.177.244.7).[m
[m
       Declarations  are used to describe the topology of the network, to describe clients on the network, to provide[m
       addresses that can be assigned to clients, or to apply a group of parameters to a group of  declarations.   In[m
       any  group  of  parameters  and  declarations,  all parameters must be specified before any declarations which[m
       depend on those parameters may be specified.[m
[m
       Declarations about network topology include the [4mshared-network[24m and the [4msubnet[24m declarations.  If clients  on  a[m
       subnet  are  to  be assigned addresses dynamically, a [4mrange[24m declaration must appear within the [4msubnet[24m declara‚Äê[m
       tion.  For clients with statically assigned addresses, or for installations where only known clients  will  be[m
       served, each such client must have a [4mhost[24m declaration.  If parameters are to be applied to a group of declara‚Äê[m
       tions which are not related strictly on a per-subnet basis, the [4mgroup[24m declaration can be used.[m
[m
       For every subnet which will be served, and for every subnet to which the dhcp server is connected, there  must[m
       be  one  [4msubnet[24m  declaration,  which tells dhcpd how to recognize that an address is on that subnet.  A [4msubnet[24m[m
       declaration is required for each subnet even if no addresses will be dynamically allocated on that subnet.[m
[m
       Some installations have physical networks on which more than one IP subnet operates.  For example, if there is[m
       a site-wide requirement that 8-bit subnet masks be used, but a department with a single physical ethernet net‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K44[K[1;1Hdhcpd.conf(5)                                    File Formats Manual                                    dhcpd.conf(5)[m
