       The [4mddns-rev-domainname[24m statement[m
[m
         [1mddns-rev-domainname[0m [4mname[24m[1m;[0m The [4mname[24m parameter should be the domain name that will be appended to the client's[m
         reversed IP address to produce a name for use in  the  client's  PTR  record.   By  default,  this  is  "in-[m
         addr.arpa.", but the default can be overridden here.[m
[m
         The  reversed  IP  address  to which this domain name is appended is always the IP address of the client, in[m
         dotted quad notation, reversed - for example, if the IP address assigned to the client is 10.17.92.74,  then[m
         the  reversed IP address is 74.92.17.10.  So a client with that IP address would, by default, be given a PTR[m
         record of 10.17.92.74.in-addr.arpa.[m
[m
       The [4mddns-update-style[24m parameter[m
[m
         [1mddns-update-style[0m [4mstyle[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
         The [4mstyle[24m parameter must be one of [1mstandard[0m, [1minterim[0m or [1mnone[0m.  The [4mddns-update-style[24m statement is only mean‚Äê[m
         ingful  in the outer scope - it is evaluated once after reading the dhcpd.conf file, rather than each time a[m
         client is assigned an IP address, so there is no way to  use  different  DNS  update  styles  for  different[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 1351/1945 71% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K...skipping...
         [4mTime[24m should be the length in [7mseconds[27m that will be assigned to a lease if the  client  requesting  the  lease[m
         does  not  ask  for  a specific expiration time.  This is used for both DHCPv4 and DHCPv6 leases (it is also[m
         known as the "valid lifetime" in DHCPv6).  The default is 43200 [7mseconds[27m.[m
[m
       The [4mdelayed-ack[24m and [4mmax-ack-delay[24m statements[m
[m
         [1mdelayed-ack[0m [4mcount[24m[1m;[0m [1mmax-ack-delay[0m [4mmicro[24m[4m[7mseconds[27m[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
         [4mCount[24m should be an integer value from zero to 2^16-1, and defaults to 28.  The  count  represents  how  many[m
         DHCPv4  replies  maximum  will  be queued pending transmission until after a database commit event.  If this[m
         number is reached, a database commit event (commonly resulting in fsync()  and  representing  a  performance[m
         penalty)  will be made, and the reply packets will be transmitted in a batch afterwards.  This preserves the[m
         RFC2131 direction that "stable storage" be updated prior to replying to clients.  Should the DHCPv4  sockets[m
         "go  dry" (select() returns immediately with no read sockets), the commit is made and any queued packets are[m
         transmitted.[m
[m
         Similarly, [4mmicro[24m[4m[7mseconds[27m[24m indicates how many micro[7mseconds[27m are permitted to pass  inbetween  queuing  a  packet[m
         pending  an  fsync,  and performing the fsync.  Valid values range from 0 to 2^32-1, and defaults to 250,000[m
         (1/4 of a second).[m
[m
         Please note that as delayed-ack is currently experimental, the delayed-ack feature is  not  compiled  in  by[m
         default, but must be enabled at compile time with ¬¥./configure --enable-delayed-ack¬¥.[m

       The [4mdo-forward-updates[24m statement[m
[m
         [1mdo-forward-updates[0m [4mflag[24m[1m;[0m[m

         The  [4mdo-forward-updates[24m statement instructs the DHCP server as to whether it should attempt to update a DHCP[m
         client¬¥s A record when the client acquires or renews a lease.  This  statement  has  no  effect  unless  DNS[m
         updates  are enabled.  Forward updates are enabled by default.  If this statement is used to disable forward[m
         updates, the DHCP server will never attempt to update the client¬¥s A record, and will only ever  attempt  to[m
         update  the client¬¥s PTR record if the client supplies an FQDN that should be placed in the PTR record using[m
         the [1mfqdn[0m option.  If forward updates are enabled, the DHCP server  will  still  honor  the  setting  of  the[m
         [1mclient-updates[0m flag.[m

       The [4mdynamic-bootp-lease-cutoff[24m statement[m

         number  of  [7mseconds[27m.  If a client reboots using BOOTP during the timeout period, the lease duration is reset[m

         parameter should be adjusted with extreme caution.[m

       The [4mfixed-address[24m declaration[m

[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 1464/1945 77% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K...skipping...
         [4mTime[24m  should be the maximum length in [7mseconds[27m that will be assigned to a lease.  If not defined, the default[m
         maximum lease time is 86400.  The only exception to this is that Dynamic BOOTP lease lengths, which are  not[m
         specified by the client, are not limited by this maximum.[m
[m
       The [4mmin-lease-time[24m statement[m
[m
         [1mmin-lease-time[0m [4mtime[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
         [4mTime[24m  should  be the minimum length in [7mseconds[27m that will be assigned to a lease.  The default is the minimum[m
         of 300 [7mseconds[27m or [1mmax-lease-time[0m.[m
[m
       The [4mmin-secs[24m statement[m
[m
         [1mmin-secs[0m [4m[7mseconds[27m[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
         [4m[7mSeconds[27m[24m should be the minimum number of [7mseconds[27m since a client began trying to acquire a  new  lease  before[m
         the DHCP server will respond to its request.  The number of [7mseconds[27m is based on what the client reports, and[m
         the maximum value that the client can report is 255 [7mseconds[27m.  Generally, setting this to one will result  in[m
         the DHCP server not responding to the client's first request, but always responding to its second request.[m
[m
         This  can be used to set up a secondary DHCP server which never offers an address to a client until the pri‚Äê[m
         mary server has been given a chance to do so.  If the primary server is down, the client will  bind  to  the[m
         secondary  server,  but  otherwise  clients  should always bind to the primary.  Note that this does not, by[m
         itself, permit a primary server and a secondary server to share a pool of dynamically-allocatable addresses.[m
[m
       The [4mnext-server[24m statement[m
[m
         [1mnext-server[0m [4mserver-name[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
         The [4mnext-server[24m statement is used to specify the host address of the server from which the initial boot file[m
         (specified  in  the  [4mfilename[24m  statement)  is to be loaded.  [4mServer-name[24m should be a numeric IP address or a[m
         domain name.  If no [4mnext-server[24m statement applies to a given client, the address 0.0.0.0 is used.[m
[m
       The [4momapi-port[24m statement[m
[m
         [1momapi-port[0m [4mport[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 1618/1945 85% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K         The [4momapi-port[24m statement causes the DHCP server to listen for OMAPI connections on the specified port.  This[m
         statement  is  required  to  enable the OMAPI protocol, which is used to examine and modify the state of the[m
         DHCP server as it is running.[m
[m
       The [4mone-lease-per-client[24m statement[m
[m
         [1mone-lease-per-client[0m [4mflag[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 1626/1945 85% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K         If this flag is enabled, whenever a client sends a DHCPREQUEST for a particular lease, the server will auto‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 1627/1945 85% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K         matically  free  any other leases the client holds.  This presumes that when the client sends a DHCPREQUEST,[m
         it has forgotten any lease not mentioned in the DHCPREQUEST - i.e., the client has  only  a  single  network[m
         interface  [4mand[24m  it  does not remember leases it's holding on networks to which it is not currently attached.[m
         Neither of these assumptions are guaranteed or provable, so we urge caution in the use of this statement.[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 1631/1945 86% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K[m
       The [4mpid-file-name[24m statement[m

            [1mping-timeout[0m [4m[7mseconds[27m[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
            If  the DHCP server determined it should send an ICMP echo request (a [4mping[24m) because the ping-check state‚Äê[m
            ment is true, ping-timeout allows you to configure how many [7mseconds[27m the DHCP server should  wait  for  an[m
            ICMP Echo response to be heard, if no ICMP Echo response has been received before the timeout expires, it[m
            assigns the address.  If a response [4mis[24m heard, the lease is abandoned, and the server does not respond  to[m
            the client.  If no value is set, ping-timeout defaults to 1 second.[m
[m
         The [4mpreferred-lifetime[24m statement[m
[m
            [1mpreferred-lifetime[0m [4m[7mseconds[27m[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
            IPv6  addresses  have  ¬¥valid¬¥ and ¬¥preferred¬¥ lifetimes.  The valid lifetime determines at what point at[m
            lease might be said to have expired, and is no longer useable.  A preferred lifetime is an advisory  con‚Äê[m
            dition  to  help  applications  move  off of the address and onto currently valid addresses (should there[m
            still be any open TCP sockets or similar).[m
[m
            The preferred lifetime defaults to the renew+rebind timers, or 3/4 the default lease time  if  none  were[m
            specified.[m
[m
         The [4mremote-port[24m statement[m
[m
            [1mremote-port[0m [4mport[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
            This statement causes the DHCP server to transmit DHCP responses to DHCP clients upon the UDP port speci‚Äê[m
            fied in [4mport[24m, rather than on port 68.  In the event that the UDP response is transmitted to a DHCP Relay,[m
            the  server  generally  uses  the  [1mlocal-port[0m  configuration  value.   Should the DHCP Relay happen to be[m
            addressed as 127.0.0.1, however, the DHCP Server transmits its response to the [1mremote-port[0m  configuration[m
            value.  This is generally only useful for testing purposes, and this configuration value should generally[m
            not be used.[m
[m
         The [4mserver-identifier[24m statement[m
[m
            [1mserver-identifier[0m [4mhostname[24m[1m;[0m[m
[m
            The server-identifier statement can be used to define the value that is sent in the DHCP  Server  Identi‚Äê[m
            fier  option  for a given scope.  The value specified [1mmust[0m be an IP address for the DHCP server, and must[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 1704/1945 90% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K            be reachable by all clients served by a particular scope.[m
[m
            The use of the server-identifier statement is not recommended - the only reason to use it is to  force  a[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 1707/1945 90% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K            value  other  than  the default value to be sent on occasions where the default value would be incorrect.[m
            The default value is the first IP address associated with the physical network  interface  on  which  the[m
            request arrived.[m
[m
            The  usual  case  where the [4mserver-identifier[24m statement needs to be sent is when a physical interface has[m
            more than one IP address, and the one being sent by default isn¬¥t appropriate for  some  or  all  clients[m
            served  by  that  interface.  Another common case is when an alias is defined for the purpose of having a[m

[?1049h[?1h=dhcpd.conf(5)                                    File Formats Manual                                    dhcpd.conf(5)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       dhcpd.conf - dhcpd configuration file[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       The dhcpd.conf file contains configuration information for [4mdhcpd,[24m the Internet Systems Consortium DHCP Server.[m
[m
       The  dhcpd.conf  file is a free-form ASCII text file.  It is parsed by the recursive-descent parser built into[m
       dhcpd.  The file may contain extra tabs and newlines for formatting purposes.  Keywords in the file are  case-[m
       insensitive.  Comments may be placed anywhere within the file (except within quotes).  Comments begin with the[m
       # character and end at the end of the line.[m
[m
       The file essentially consists of a list of statements.  Statements fall into two broad categories - parameters[m
       and declarations.[m
[m
       Parameter statements either say how to do something (e.g., how long a lease to offer), whether to do something[m
       (e.g., should dhcpd provide addresses to unknown clients), or what parameters to provide to the client  (e.g.,[m
       use gateway 220.177.244.7).[m
[m
       Declarations  are used to describe the topology of the network, to describe clients on the network, to provide[m
       addresses that can be assigned to clients, or to apply a group of parameters to a group of  declarations.   In[m
       any  group  of  parameters  and  declarations,  all parameters must be specified before any declarations which[m
       depend on those parameters may be specified.[m
[m
       Declarations about network topology include the [4mshared-network[24m and the [4msubnet[24m declarations.  If clients  on  a[m
       subnet  are  to  be assigned addresses dynamically, a [4mrange[24m declaration must appear within the [4msubnet[24m declara‚Äê[m
       tion.  For clients with statically assigned addresses, or for installations where only known clients  will  be[m
       served, each such client must have a [4mhost[24m declaration.  If parameters are to be applied to a group of declara‚Äê[m
       tions which are not related strictly on a per-subnet basis, the [4mgroup[24m declaration can be used.[m
[m
       For every subnet which will be served, and for every subnet to which the dhcp server is connected, there  must[m
       be  one  [4msubnet[24m  declaration,  which tells dhcpd how to recognize that an address is on that subnet.  A [4msubnet[24m[m
       declaration is required for each subnet even if no addresses will be dynamically allocated on that subnet.[m
[m
       Some installations have physical networks on which more than one IP subnet operates.  For example, if there is[m
       a site-wide requirement that 8-bit subnet masks be used, but a department with a single physical ethernet net‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       work expands to the point where it has more than 254 nodes, it may be necessary to run two  8-bit  subnets  on[m
       the  same  ethernet until such time as a new physical network can be added.  In this case, the [4msubnet[24m declara‚Äê[m
       tions for these two networks must be enclosed in a [4mshared-network[24m declaration.[m
[m
       Note that even when the [4mshared-network[24m declaration is absent, an empty one is created by the server to contain[m
       the  [4msubnet[24m  (and  any  scoped  parameters  included  in the [4msubnet[24m).  For practical purposes, this means that[m
       "stateless" DHCP clients, which are not tied to addresses (and therefore subnets) will receive the  same  con‚Äê[m
       figuration as stateful ones.[m
[m
       Some  sites  may have departments which have clients on more than one subnet, but it may be desirable to offer[m
       those clients a uniform set of parameters which are different than what would be offered to clients from other[m
       departments  on  the same subnet.  For clients which will be declared explicitly with [4mhost[24m declarations, these[m
       declarations can be enclosed in a [4mgroup[24m declaration along with the parameters which are common to that depart‚Äê[m
       ment.   For  clients whose addresses will be dynamically assigned, class declarations and conditional declara‚Äê[m
       tions may be used to group parameter assignments based on information the client sends.[m
[m
       When a client is to be booted, its boot parameters are determined by consulting that client's [4mhost[24m declaration[m
       (if  any),  and  then  consulting any [4mclass[24m declarations matching the client, followed by the [4mpool[24m, [4msubnet[24m and[m
       [4mshared-network[24m declarations for the IP address assigned to the client.   Each  of  these  declarations  itself[m
       appears  within  a  lexical scope, and all declarations at less specific lexical scopes are also consulted for[m
       client option declarations.  Scopes are never considered twice, and if parameters are declared  in  more  than[m
       one scope, the parameter declared in the most specific scope is the one that is used.[m
[m
       When  dhcpd  tries  to find a [4mhost[24m declaration for a client, it first looks for a [4mhost[24m declaration which has a[m
       [4mfixed-address[24m declaration that lists an IP address that is valid for the subnet or shared network on which the[m
       client  is  booting.   If it doesn't find any such entry, it tries to find an entry which has no [4mfixed-address[24m[m
       declaration.[m
[m
[1mEXAMPLES[0m[m
       A typical dhcpd.conf file will look something like this:[m
[m
       [4mglobal[24m [4mparameters...[24m[m
[m
       subnet 204.254.239.0 netmask 255.255.255.224 {[m
         [4msubnet-specific[24m [4mparameters...[24m[m
         range 204.254.239.10 204.254.239.30;[m
       }[m

[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 43 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K         range 204.254.239.42 204.254.239.62;[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 44 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       }[m

[?1049h[?1h=dhcpd.conf(5)                                    File Formats Manual                                    dhcpd.conf(5)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       dhcpd.conf - dhcpd configuration file[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       The dhcpd.conf file contains configuration information for [4mdhcpd,[24m the Internet Systems Consortium DHCP Server.[m
[m
       The  dhcpd.conf  file is a free-form ASCII text file.  It is parsed by the recursive-descent parser built into[m
       dhcpd.  The file may contain extra tabs and newlines for formatting purposes.  Keywords in the file are  case-[m
       insensitive.  Comments may be placed anywhere within the file (except within quotes).  Comments begin with the[m
       # character and end at the end of the line.[m
[m
       The file essentially consists of a list of statements.  Statements fall into two broad categories - parameters[m
       and declarations.[m
[m
       Parameter statements either say how to do something (e.g., how long a lease to offer), whether to do something[m
       (e.g., should dhcpd provide addresses to unknown clients), or what parameters to provide to the client  (e.g.,[m
       use gateway 220.177.244.7).[m
[m
       Declarations  are used to describe the topology of the network, to describe clients on the network, to provide[m
       addresses that can be assigned to clients, or to apply a group of parameters to a group of  declarations.   In[m
       any  group  of  parameters  and  declarations,  all parameters must be specified before any declarations which[m
       depend on those parameters may be specified.[m
[m
       Declarations about network topology include the [4mshared-network[24m and the [4msubnet[24m declarations.  If clients  on  a[m
       subnet  are  to  be assigned addresses dynamically, a [4mrange[24m declaration must appear within the [4msubnet[24m declara‚Äê[m
       tion.  For clients with statically assigned addresses, or for installations where only known clients  will  be[m
       served, each such client must have a [4mhost[24m declaration.  If parameters are to be applied to a group of declara‚Äê[m
       tions which are not related strictly on a per-subnet basis, the [4mgroup[24m declaration can be used.[m
[m
       For every subnet which will be served, and for every subnet to which the dhcp server is connected, there  must[m
       be  one  [4msubnet[24m  declaration,  which tells dhcpd how to recognize that an address is on that subnet.  A [4msubnet[24m[m
       declaration is required for each subnet even if no addresses will be dynamically allocated on that subnet.[m
[m
       Some installations have physical networks on which more than one IP subnet operates.  For example, if there is[m
       a site-wide requirement that 8-bit subnet masks be used, but a department with a single physical ethernet net‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       work expands to the point where it has more than 254 nodes, it may be necessary to run two  8-bit  subnets  on[m
       the  same  ethernet until such time as a new physical network can be added.  In this case, the [4msubnet[24m declara‚Äê[m
       tions for these two networks must be enclosed in a [4mshared-network[24m declaration.[m
[m
       Note that even when the [4mshared-network[24m declaration is absent, an empty one is created by the server to contain[m
       the  [4msubnet[24m  (and  any  scoped  parameters  included  in the [4msubnet[24m).  For practical purposes, this means that[m
       "stateless" DHCP clients, which are not tied to addresses (and therefore subnets) will receive the  same  con‚Äê[m
       figuration as stateful ones.[m
[m
       Some  sites  may have departments which have clients on more than one subnet, but it may be desirable to offer[m
       those clients a uniform set of parameters which are different than what would be offered to clients from other[m
       departments  on  the same subnet.  For clients which will be declared explicitly with [4mhost[24m declarations, these[m
       declarations can be enclosed in a [4mgroup[24m declaration along with the parameters which are common to that depart‚Äê[m
       ment.   For  clients whose addresses will be dynamically assigned, class declarations and conditional declara‚Äê[m
       tions may be used to group parameter assignments based on information the client sends.[m
[m
       When a client is to be booted, its boot parameters are determined by consulting that client's [4mhost[24m declaration[m
       (if  any),  and  then  consulting any [4mclass[24m declarations matching the client, followed by the [4mpool[24m, [4msubnet[24m and[m
       [4mshared-network[24m declarations for the IP address assigned to the client.   Each  of  these  declarations  itself[m
       appears  within  a  lexical scope, and all declarations at less specific lexical scopes are also consulted for[m
       client option declarations.  Scopes are never considered twice, and if parameters are declared  in  more  than[m
       one scope, the parameter declared in the most specific scope is the one that is used.[m
[m
       When  dhcpd  tries  to find a [4mhost[24m declaration for a client, it first looks for a [4mhost[24m declaration which has a[m
       [4mfixed-address[24m declaration that lists an IP address that is valid for the subnet or shared network on which the[m
       client  is  booting.   If it doesn't find any such entry, it tries to find an entry which has no [4mfixed-address[24m[m
       declaration.[m
[m
[1mEXAMPLES[0m[m

         [4msubnet-specific[24m [4mparameters...[24m[m

       }[m

       As you can see in Figure 2, you can specify host addresses in parameters using their domain names rather  than[m
       their  numeric  IP  addresses.  If a given hostname resolves to more than one IP address (for example, if that[m
       host has two ethernet interfaces), then where possible, both addresses are supplied to the client.[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 78 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 79 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K       The most obvious reason for having [7msubnet[27m-specific parameters as shown in Figure 1 is  that  each  [7msubnet[27m,  of[m
       necessity, has its own router.  So for the first [7msubnet[27m, for example, there should be something like:[m
[m
            option routers 204.254.239.1;[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 83 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 84 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K       Note  that  the  address here is specified numerically.  This is not required - if you have a different domain[m
       name for each interface on your router, it's perfectly legitimate to use the domain name  for  that  interface[m
       instead  of  the  numeric  address.   However,  in  many  cases there may be only one domain name for all of a[m
       router's IP addresses, and it would not be appropriate to use that name here.[m
[m
       In Figure 1 there is also a [4mgroup[24m statement, which provides common parameters for  a  set  of  three  hosts  -[m
       zappo,  beppo  and  harpo.   As  you can see, these hosts are all in the test.isc.org domain, so it might make[m
       sense for a group-specific parameter to override the domain name supplied to these hosts:[m
[m
            option domain-name "test.isc.org";[m
[m
       Also, given the domain they're in, these are probably test machines.  If we wanted to test  the  DHCP  leasing[m
       mechanism, we might set the lease timeout somewhat shorter than the default:[m
[m
            max-lease-time 120;[m
            default-lease-time 120;[m
[m
       You may have noticed that while some parameters start with the [4moption[24m keyword, some do not.  Parameters start‚Äê[m
       ing with the [4moption[24m keyword correspond to actual DHCP options, while parameters that do  not  start  with  the[m
       option keyword either control the behavior of the DHCP server (e.g., how long a lease dhcpd will give out), or[m
       specify client parameters that are not optional in the DHCP protocol (for example, server-name and filename).[m
[m
       In Figure 1, each host had [4mhost-specific[24m [4mparameters[24m.  These could include such things as the [4mhostname[24m  option,[m
       the  name  of a file to upload (the [4mfilename[24m parameter) and the address of the server from which to upload the[m
       file (the [4mnext-server[24m parameter).  In general, any parameter can appear anywhere that parameters are  allowed,[m
       and will be applied according to the scope in which the parameter appears.[m
[m
       Imagine  that you have a site with a lot of NCD X-Terminals.  These terminals come in a variety of models, and[m
       you want to specify the boot files for each model.  One way to do this would be to have host declarations  for[m
       each server and group them by model:[m
[m
       group {[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 117 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K         filename "Xncd19r";[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 118 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K...skipping...
       pool of addresses, even on the same network segment or [7msubnet[27m.  For example, you may want to provide  a  large[m
       set of addresses that can be assigned to DHCP clients that are registered to your DHCP server, while providing[m
       a smaller set of addresses, possibly with short lease times, that are available for unknown clients.   If  you[m
       have  a firewall, you may be able to arrange for addresses from one pool to be allowed access to the Internet,[m
       while addresses in another pool are not, thus encouraging users to register their DHCP clients.  To  do  this,[m
       you would set up a pair of pool declarations:[m
[m
       [7msubnet[27m 10.0.0.0 netmask 255.255.255.0 {[m
         option routers 10.0.0.254;[m
[m
         # Unknown clients get this pool.[m
         pool {[m
           option domain-name-servers bogus.example.com;[m
           max-lease-time 300;[m
           range 10.0.0.200 10.0.0.253;[m
           allow unknown-clients;[m
         }[m
[m
         # Known clients get this pool.[m
         pool {[m
           option domain-name-servers ns1.example.com, ns2.example.com;[m
           max-lease-time 28800;[m
           range 10.0.0.5 10.0.0.199;[m
           deny unknown-clients;[m
         }[m
       }[m
[m
       It  is  also possible to set up entirely different [7msubnet[27ms for known and unknown clients - address pools exist[m
       at the level of shared networks, so address ranges within pool declarations can be on different [7msubnet[27ms.[m
[m
       As you can see in the preceding example, pools can have permit lists that control which  clients  are  allowed[m
       access  to the pool and which aren't.  Each entry in a pool's permit list is introduced with the [4mallow[24m or [4mdeny[24m[m
       keyword.  If a pool has a permit list, then only those clients that match specific entries on the permit  list[m
       will  be  eligible to be assigned addresses from the pool.  If a pool has a deny list, then only those clients[m
       that do not match any entries on the deny list will be eligible.   If both permit and deny lists exist  for  a[m
       pool, then only clients that match the permit list and do not match the deny list will be allowed access.[m
[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 181 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K[1mDYNAMIC[0m [1mADDRESS[0m [1mALLOCATION[0m[m
       Address  allocation  is actually only done when a client is in the INIT state and has sent a DHCPDISCOVER mes‚Äê[m
       sage.  If the client thinks it has a valid lease and sends a DHCPREQUEST to initiate or renew that lease,  the[m
       server  has  only  three  choices - it can ignore the DHCPREQUEST, send a DHCPNAK to tell the client it should[m
       stop using the address, or send a DHCPACK, telling the client to go ahead and use the address for a while.[m
[m
       If the server finds the address the client is requesting, and that address is available  to  the  client,  the[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 188 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K       server  will send a DHCPACK.  If the address is no longer available, or the client isn't permitted to have it,[m
       the server will send a DHCPNAK.  If the server knows nothing about the address, it will remain silent,  unless[m
       the  address  is  incorrect  for  the  network segment to which the client has been attached and the server is[m
       authoritative for that network segment, in which case the server will send a DHCPNAK even  though  it  doesn't[m
       know about the address.[m
[m
       There  may  be  a  host declaration matching the client's identification.  If that host declaration contains a[m
       fixed-address declaration that lists an IP address that is valid for the network segment to which  the  client[m
       is  connected.   In  this  case,  the DHCP server will never do dynamic address allocation.  In this case, the[m
       client is [4mrequired[24m to take the address specified in the host declaration.  If the client sends  a  DHCPREQUEST[m
       for some other address, the server will respond with a DHCPNAK.[m
[m
       When  the DHCP server allocates a new address for a client (remember, this only happens if the client has sent[m
       a DHCPDISCOVER), it first looks to see if the client already has a valid lease on an IP address, or  if  there[m
       is  an  old  IP  address the client had before that hasn't yet been reassigned.  In that case, the server will[m
       take that address and check it to see if the client is still permitted to use it.  If the client is no  longer[m
       permitted  to  use it, the lease is freed if the server thought it was still in use - the fact that the client[m
       has sent a DHCPDISCOVER proves to the server that the client is no longer using the lease.[m
[m
       If no existing lease is found, or if the client is forbidden to receive the existing lease,  then  the  server[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 208 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K       will  look  in  the  list of address pools for the network segment to which the client is attached for a lease[m
[7m Manual page dhcpd.conf(5) line 209 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K...skipping...
       [7msubnet[27m 10.0.0.0 netmask 255.255.255.0 {[m
         pool {[m
           allow members of "allocation-class-1";[m
           range 10.0.0.11 10.0.0.50;[m
         }[m
         pool {[m
           allow members of "allocation-class-2";[m
           range 10.0.0.51 10.0.0.100;[m
         }[m
       }[m
[m
       The data following the class name in the subclass declaration is a constant value to use in matching the match[m
       expression for the class.  When class matching is done, the server will evaluate the match expression and then[m
       look the result up in the hash table.  If it finds a match, the client is considered  a  member  of  both  the[m
       class and the subclass.[m
[m
       Subclasses  can  be declared with or without scope.  In the above example, the sole purpose of the subclass is[m
       to allow some clients access to one address pool, while other clients are given access to the other  pool,  so[m
       these subclasses are declared without scopes.  If part of the purpose of the subclass were to define different[m
       parameter values for some clients, you might want to declare some subclasses with scopes.[m
[m
       In the above example, if you had a single client that needed some configuration parameters, while most didn't,[m
       you might write the following subclass declaration for that client:[m
[m
       subclass "allocation-class-2" 1:08:00:2b:a1:11:31 {[m
         option root-path "samsara:/var/diskless/alphapc";[m
         filename "/tftpboot/netbsd.alphapc-diskless";[m
       }[m
[m
       In  this  example,  we've used subclassing as a way to control address allocation on a per-client basis.  How‚Äê[m
       ever, it's also possible to use subclassing in ways that are not specific to clients - for example, to use the[m
       value  of  the  vendor-class-identifier  option  to  determine what values to send in the vendor-encapsulated-[m
       options option.  An example of this is shown under the VENDOR ENCAPSULATED OPTIONS head in the [1mdhcp-options(5)[0m[m
       manual page.[m
[m

       You  may  specify a limit to the number of clients in a class that can be assigned leases.  The effect of this[m

     List of control groups that the daemon will be run in. For example,
     CGROUP_DAEMON="cpu:daemons cpuacct:/" will run it in the daemons
     group for the CPU controller, and the '/' group for the CPU accounting

Files in /etc/sysconfig/[7mnetwork-scripts[27m/
========================================

/etc/sysconfig/[7mnetwork-scripts[27m/ifup:
/etc/sysconfig/[7mnetwork-scripts[27m/ifdown:

  Symlinks to /sbin/ifup and /sbin/ifdown, respectively.
  These are the only two scripts "in" this directory that should
  be called directly; these two scripts call all the other
  scripts as needed.  These symlinks are here for legacy purposes --
  only /sbin/ifup and /sbin/ifdown should currently be used
  at the user level.

  These scripts take one argument normally: the name of the device
  (e.g. eth0).  They are called with a second argument of "boot"
  during the boot sequence so that devices that are not meant to
  be brought up on boot (ONBOOT=no, see below) can be ignored at
  that time.

  Also, interfaces may be brought up via the hotplug scripts;
  in this case, HOTPLUG=no needs to be set to no to avoid this.
  This is useful e.g. to prevent bonding device activation by merely
  loading the bonding kernel module.
